https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302281040   Functions may be qualified as async, and this can also be combined with the
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302281088   `unsafe` qualifier:
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302287965   Async functions do no work when called: instead, they
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302288047   capture their arguments into a future. When polled, that future will
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302288060   execute the function's body.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302288375   An async function is roughly equivalent to a function
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302288619   The actual desugaring is
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289197   - The return type in the desugaring is assumed to capture all lifetime
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289322   x.len()
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289463   async move { x.len() }
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289702   desugared example above, which explicitly outlives, and hence
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289742   captures, `'a`.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289916   that returns `impl Future` and with an `async move` block as its body:
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302290161   - The `async move` in the body captures otherwise
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302290240   unused function parameters. This ensures that function
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302291537   a *future*. The final expression of the block, if present, determines
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302292881   this type is unspecified, but it is roughly equivalent to an enum with
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302293005   Executing an async block is similar to executing a closure
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302293738   one variant per `await` point such that the data needed to
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302293767   resume from that point is stored.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302295477   `Copy` type, async blocks will capture a shared reference to the variable. If
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302295689   the variable is mutated, they will capture a mutable reference.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302295893   Finally, if the variable is moved, async blocks will capture the variable "by
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302296103   future, no matter how they are used.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302296651   ### Capture modes
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302296790   ### <Invent some title>
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302297191   The bodies of async blocks can contain `await` expressions. These
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302297576   ready. See the section on [await expressions] for more details.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302298328   Async blocks are considered a sort of
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302298566   break; // This would break out of the loop.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299110   is to "suspend" the current computation until the given future is ready
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299530   More specifically, an `<expr>.await` expression has the following effect.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299676   1. Evaluate `f` to a future `tmp` using the `IntoFuture::into_future` method;
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299748   2. Pin `tmp` using `Pin::new_unchecked`;
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299897   3. This pinned future is then polled by calling the [`Future::poll`] method and
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300033   3. If the result evaluates to `Poll::Pending`, then the future returns
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300254   `Poll::Pending`, suspending its state so that, when re-polled,    execution resumes at step 2;
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300318   4. If the result evaluates to `Poll::Ready`, then the result is used as the result
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300355   of the `await` expression itself.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300610   ## Task context
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300717   current async context when it itself was polled. Because `await`
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300907   Effectively, an `f.await` expression is roughly
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302317097   1. evaluate `f` to a future temporary variable `tmp` using the `IntoFuture:into_future` method;
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302782998   referenced variables into the resulting future.

With continuous development of Gardener, over the time its architecture and API might have to be changed to reduce complexity and support more features. In this process developers are bound to keep Gardener version backward compatible with last two releases. But maintaining backward compatibility is quite complex and effortful tasks. So, to save short term complex effort, its common practice in open source community to use work around or hacky solutions sometimes. This results in rare issues which are supposed to be resolved by human interaction across upgrades of Gardener version.

https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251140581   Unfortunately, in CouchDB, when we read from either of these indexes, it
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251141663   up the number of shards, every index request must perform more work.
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251141789   Fortunately for you, dear reader, partitioned databases were created to solve
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251141976   In the previous section, we introduced a hypothetical database that contains
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251142191   use case, it's quite logical to group all documents by their ``sensor_id``
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251142285   field. In this case, we would call the ``sensor_id`` the partition.
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251142882   gigabytes of data. Which, for the example of sensor documents, equates to roughly
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251143166   By using partitions, we can execute queries against these individual groups
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251143274   shard on disk. Thus, the view engine only has to consult one copy of the
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251143764   given shard range when executing a query instead of executing
https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385 https://github.com/apache/couchdb-documentation/pull/385#discussion_r251143786   the query across all ``Q`` shards in the database.

https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310756420   So all you need to know is that vim is a text editor. In my opinion one of vim's strengths comes with how flexible it can be. It can be as simple or complex as you wish. It can be used to edit a simple config file on a server or you can make it a complete code editing environment.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310756668   In this blog post I'll show you the basics of vim and provide you with the smallest amount of knowledge necessary to make vim useful for yourself, and yes I'll teach you how to exit ;)
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310756748   I'll assume you already have vim installed, if you are on a \*nix system you probably already have it.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310756845   You'll see something like the following:
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310757485   Vim is a "modal editor", which means vim will behave different depending on which mode you are currently on.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310757662   I'll introduce you to three basic modes. **NORMAL**, **INSERT** and **VISUAL**. There are a couple more, but these are the basics ones, and they are all you need to know for now.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310757747   ## NORMAL - The default vim mode
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310757976   In this mode you'll do things like navigate through your text file, removing, copying and pasting text.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310758075   While you are in **NORMAL** mode you would need to move around your text file. These are the basics commands that will help you achieve that.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310758427   p  - paste to the line underneath.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310758587   You probably were wondering, how do I actually write something into vim, well... this is the mode where you can do that.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310758821   You enter INSERT mode by pressing the letter `i`. In this mode you'll use your keyboard like in any other editor, vim will not behave in a special way when you are in this mode.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310759024   * :q! - Quit vim even if your changes were not saved.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310759253   You could select a paragraph, a single word or even a letter and apply commands to that selected piece of text. You could copy(yy) a selection of text or delete (dd) it if you wish. To exit visual mode you press `ESC` and will return to **NORMAL** mode.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310759342   These are a couple of resources that can help you improve your vim skills.
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310759475   * :h :help                   - vim go to help command
https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194 https://github.com/ombulabs/blog/pull/194#discussion_r310759621   This is a really basic introduction to vim and it's just the tip of the iceberg of what vim really can do. https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302281040   Functions may be qualified as async, and this can also be combined with the
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302281088   `unsafe` qualifier:
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302287965   Async functions do no work when called: instead, they
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302288047   capture their arguments into a future. When polled, that future will
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302288060   execute the function's body.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302288375   An async function is roughly equivalent to a function
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302288619   The actual desugaring is
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289197   - The return type in the desugaring is assumed to capture all lifetime
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289322   x.len()
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289463   async move { x.len() }
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289702   desugared example above, which explicitly outlives, and hence
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289742   captures, `'a`.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302289916   that returns `impl Future` and with an `async move` block as its body:
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302290161   - The `async move` in the body captures otherwise
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302290240   unused function parameters. This ensures that function
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302291537   a *future*. The final expression of the block, if present, determines
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302292881   this type is unspecified, but it is roughly equivalent to an enum with
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302293005   Executing an async block is similar to executing a closure
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302293738   one variant per `await` point such that the data needed to
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302293767   resume from that point is stored.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302295477   `Copy` type, async blocks will capture a shared reference to the variable. If
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302295689   the variable is mutated, they will capture a mutable reference.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302295893   Finally, if the variable is moved, async blocks will capture the variable "by
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302296103   future, no matter how they are used.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302296651   ### Capture modes
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302296790   ### <Invent some title>
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302297191   The bodies of async blocks can contain `await` expressions. These
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302297576   ready. See the section on [await expressions] for more details.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302298328   Async blocks are considered a sort of
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302298566   break; // This would break out of the loop.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299110   is to "suspend" the current computation until the given future is ready
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299530   More specifically, an `<expr>.await` expression has the following effect.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299676   1. Evaluate `f` to a future `tmp` using the `IntoFuture::into_future` method;
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299748   2. Pin `tmp` using `Pin::new_unchecked`;
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302299897   3. This pinned future is then polled by calling the [`Future::poll`] method and
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300033   3. If the result evaluates to `Poll::Pending`, then the future returns
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300254   `Poll::Pending`, suspending its state so that, when re-polled,    execution resumes at step 2;
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300318   4. If the result evaluates to `Poll::Ready`, then the result is used as the result
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300355   of the `await` expression itself.
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300610   ## Task context
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300717   current async context when it itself was polled. Because `await`
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302300907   Effectively, an `f.await` expression is roughly
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302317097   1. evaluate `f` to a future temporary variable `tmp` using the `IntoFuture:into_future` method;
https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r302782998   referenced variables into the resulting future.

https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635 https://github.com/rust-lang-nursery/reference/pull/635#discussion_r307403466   // Soundness condition: `x` must be safe to dereference until

With continuous development of Gardener, over the time its architecture and API might have to be changed to reduce complexity and support more features. In this process developers are bound to keep Gardener version backward compatible with last two releases. But maintaining backward compatibility is quite complex and effortful tasks. So, to save short term complex effort, its common practice in open source community to use work around or hacky solutions sometimes. This results in rare issues which are supposed to be resolved by human interaction across upgrades of Gardener version.
